Other Fantasy Writing Tips

Here are some final miscellaneous tips that can help you level up as a
fantasy * Prologues: Prologues are slightly controversial, as some authors
don’t like having them, but other authors insist they should be
used. Generally speaking, I recommend using them if you want to set
up the conflict and tone of the book, and if your chapter 1 doesn’t
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
fantasy fantasy settings contain only subtle magical influences. Figure out
which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
* High or Low Fantasy?: High fantasy worlds have pervasive magic. Low
fantasy which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
* Hard vs. Soft Magic Systems: Hard systems have strictly defined
in worldbuilding and storytelling. Let their triumphs inspire your
own.

fantasy fiction! It's an ambitious undertaking, but immensely fulfilling. I

Other Fantasy Writing Tips

Here are some final miscellaneous tips that can help you level up as a
fantasy * Prologues: Prologues are slightly controversial, as some authors
don’t like having them, but other authors insist they should be
used. Generally speaking, I recommend using them if you want to set
up the conflict and tone of the book, and if your chapter 1 doesn’t
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
fantasy fantasy settings contain only subtle magical influences. Figure out
which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
* High or Low Fantasy?: High fantasy worlds have pervasive magic. Low
fantasy which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
* Hard vs. Soft Magic Systems: Hard systems have strictly defined
in worldbuilding and storytelling. Let their triumphs inspire your
own.

fantasy fiction! It's an ambitious undertaking, but immensely fulfilling. I
hope these strategies help you turn the fantastical stories kindling in
your soul into fully-realized novels.

Other Fantasy Writing Tips

Here are some final miscellaneous tips that can help you level up as a
fantasy * Prologues: Prologues are slightly controversial, as some authors
don’t like having them, but other authors insist they should be
used. Generally speaking, I recommend using them if you want to set
up the conflict and tone of the book, and if your chapter 1 doesn’t
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
fantasy fantasy settings contain only subtle magical influences. Figure out
which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
* High or Low Fantasy?: High fantasy worlds have pervasive magic. Low
fantasy which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
* Hard vs. Soft Magic Systems: Hard systems have strictly defined
in worldbuilding and storytelling. Let their triumphs inspire your
own.

fantasy fiction! It's an ambitious undertaking, but immensely fulfilling. I
hope these strategies help you turn the fantastical stories kindling in
your soul into fully-realized novels.

Other Fantasy Writing Tips

Here are some final miscellaneous tips that can help you level up as a
fantasy * Prologues: Prologues are slightly controversial, as some authors
don’t like having them, but other authors insist they should be
used. Generally speaking, I recommend using them if you want to set
up the conflict and tone of the book, and if your chapter 1 doesn’t
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
fantasy fantasy settings contain only subtle magical influences. Figure out
which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
* High or Low Fantasy?: High fantasy worlds have pervasive magic. Low
fantasy which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
* Hard vs. Soft Magic Systems: Hard systems have strictly defined
in worldbuilding and storytelling. Let their triumphs inspire your
own.

fantasy fiction! It's an ambitious undertaking, but immensely fulfilling. I
hope these strategies help you turn the fantastical stories kindling in
your soul into fully-realized novels.

Other Fantasy Writing Tips

Here are some final miscellaneous tips that can help you level up as a
fantasy * Prologues: Prologues are slightly controversial, as some authors
don’t like having them, but other authors insist they should be
used. Generally speaking, I recommend using them if you want to set
up the conflict and tone of the book, and if your chapter 1 doesn’t
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
fantasy fantasy settings contain only subtle magical influences. Figure out
which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
* High or Low Fantasy?: High fantasy worlds have pervasive magic. Low
fantasy which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
* Hard vs. Soft Magic Systems: Hard systems have strictly defined
in worldbuilding and storytelling. Let their triumphs inspire your
own.

fantasy fiction! It's an ambitious undertaking, but immensely fulfilling. I
hope these strategies help you turn the fantastical stories kindling in
your soul into fully-realized novels.

Other Fantasy Writing Tips

fantasy * Prologues: Prologues are slightly controversial, as some authors

used. Generally speaking, I recommend using them if you want to set
up the conflict and tone of the book, and if your chapter 1 doesn’t
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)

in worldbuilding and storytelling. Let their triumphs inspire your

inventing a whole reality? Here's my advice:
fantasy of magic. Determine its rules, costs, limitations and how it's
harnessed. Is magic common or rare? Does using it drain life force
or sanity? Do mages invoke divine powers or manipulate natural
or sanity? Do mages invoke divine powers or manipulate natural
energies?
* Races and Creatures: Populate your world with original or
fantasy mythical beasts and monsters. Consider their appearances, powers,
temperaments, societies, histories and how they fit into the world.
Give each a distinct flair.
For more on worldbuilding, see our comprehensive article on the
subject.

fantasy

and self-discipline are what transform ideas into finished manuscripts.
Knowing someone is expecting regular updates keeps you on track.
Better still, write together at coffee shops for camaraderie.

fantasy

your diamond-in-the-rough into a dazzling gem ready to publish. Here
errors, spacing issues, etc. before publication. Double check all
names and facts.

fantasy
Here are some final miscellaneous tips that can help you level up as a
fantasy writer:
Other Fantasy Writing Tips

Here are some final miscellaneous tips that can help you level up as a
fantasy * Prologues: Prologues are slightly controversial, as some authors
don’t like having them, but other authors insist they should be
used. Generally speaking, I recommend using them if you want to set
up the conflict and tone of the book, and if your chapter 1 doesn’t
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
fantasy fantasy settings contain only subtle magical influences. Figure out
which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
* High or Low Fantasy?: High fantasy worlds have pervasive magic. Low
fantasy which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
* Hard vs. Soft Magic Systems: Hard systems have strictly defined
in worldbuilding and storytelling. Let their triumphs inspire your
own.

fantasy fiction! It's an ambitious undertaking, but immensely fulfilling. I
hope these strategies help you turn the fantastical stories kindling in
your soul into fully-realized novels.

Other Fantasy Writing Tips

Here are some final miscellaneous tips that can help you level up as a
fantasy * Prologues: Prologues are slightly controversial, as some authors
don’t like having them, but other authors insist they should be
used. Generally speaking, I recommend using them if you want to set
up the conflict and tone of the book, and if your chapter 1 doesn’t
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
fantasy fantasy settings contain only subtle magical influences. Figure out
which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
* High or Low Fantasy?: High fantasy worlds have pervasive magic. Low
fantasy which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
* Hard vs. Soft Magic Systems: Hard systems have strictly defined
in worldbuilding and storytelling. Let their triumphs inspire your
own.

fantasy fiction! It's an ambitious undertaking, but immensely fulfilling. I
hope these strategies help you turn the fantastical stories kindling in
your soul into fully-realized novels.

Other Fantasy Writing Tips

Here are some final miscellaneous tips that can help you level up as a
fantasy * Prologues: Prologues are slightly controversial, as some authors
don’t like having them, but other authors insist they should be
used. Generally speaking, I recommend using them if you want to set
up the conflict and tone of the book, and if your chapter 1 doesn’t
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
fantasy fantasy settings contain only subtle magical influences. Figure out
which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
* High or Low Fantasy?: High fantasy worlds have pervasive magic. Low
fantasy which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
* Hard vs. Soft Magic Systems: Hard systems have strictly defined
in worldbuilding and storytelling. Let their triumphs inspire your
own.

fantasy fiction! It's an ambitious undertaking, but immensely fulfilling. I
hope these strategies help you turn the fantastical stories kindling in
your soul into fully-realized novels.

fantasy of magic. Determine its rules, costs, limitations and how it's

Other Fantasy Writing Tips

Here are some final miscellaneous tips that can help you level up as a
fantasy * Prologues: Prologues are slightly controversial, as some authors
don’t like having them, but other authors insist they should be
used. Generally speaking, I recommend using them if you want to set
up the conflict and tone of the book, and if your chapter 1 doesn’t
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
fantasy fantasy settings contain only subtle magical influences. Figure out
which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
* High or Low Fantasy?: High fantasy worlds have pervasive magic. Low
fantasy which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
* Hard vs. Soft Magic Systems: Hard systems have strictly defined
in worldbuilding and storytelling. Let their triumphs inspire your
own.

fantasy fiction! It's an ambitious undertaking, but immensely fulfilling. I
hope these strategies help you turn the fantastical stories kindling in
your soul into fully-realized novels.

fantasy of magic. Determine its rules, costs, limitations and how it's

Other Fantasy Writing Tips

Here are some final miscellaneous tips that can help you level up as a
fantasy * Prologues: Prologues are slightly controversial, as some authors
don’t like having them, but other authors insist they should be
used. Generally speaking, I recommend using them if you want to set
up the conflict and tone of the book, and if your chapter 1 doesn’t
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
fantasy fantasy settings contain only subtle magical influences. Figure out
which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
* High or Low Fantasy?: High fantasy worlds have pervasive magic. Low
fantasy which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
* Hard vs. Soft Magic Systems: Hard systems have strictly defined
in worldbuilding and storytelling. Let their triumphs inspire your
own.

fantasy fiction! It's an ambitious undertaking, but immensely fulfilling. I
hope these strategies help you turn the fantastical stories kindling in
your soul into fully-realized novels.

Other Fantasy Writing Tips

fantasy * Prologues: Prologues are slightly controversial, as some authors

used. Generally speaking, I recommend using them if you want to set

do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)

in worldbuilding and storytelling. Let their triumphs inspire your
own.

Other Fantasy Writing Tips

Here are some final miscellaneous tips that can help you level up as a
fantasy * Prologues: Prologues are slightly controversial, as some authors
don’t like having them, but other authors insist they should be
used. Generally speaking, I recommend using them if you want to set
up the conflict and tone of the book, and if your chapter 1 doesn’t
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
fantasy fantasy settings contain only subtle magical influences. Figure out
which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
* High or Low Fantasy?: High fantasy worlds have pervasive magic. Low
fantasy which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
* Hard vs. Soft Magic Systems: Hard systems have strictly defined
in worldbuilding and storytelling. Let their triumphs inspire your
own.

fantasy fiction! It's an ambitious undertaking, but immensely fulfilling. I
hope these strategies help you turn the fantastical stories kindling in
your soul into fully-realized novels.

Other Fantasy Writing Tips

Here are some final miscellaneous tips that can help you level up as a
fantasy * Prologues: Prologues are slightly controversial, as some authors
don’t like having them, but other authors insist they should be
used. Generally speaking, I recommend using them if you want to set
up the conflict and tone of the book, and if your chapter 1 doesn’t
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
fantasy fantasy settings contain only subtle magical influences. Figure out
which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
* High or Low Fantasy?: High fantasy worlds have pervasive magic. Low
fantasy which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
* Hard vs. Soft Magic Systems: Hard systems have strictly defined
in worldbuilding and storytelling. Let their triumphs inspire your
own.

fantasy fiction! It's an ambitious undertaking, but immensely fulfilling. I
hope these strategies help you turn the fantastical stories kindling in
your soul into fully-realized novels.

Other Fantasy Writing Tips

Here are some final miscellaneous tips that can help you level up as a
fantasy * Prologues: Prologues are slightly controversial, as some authors
don’t like having them, but other authors insist they should be
used. Generally speaking, I recommend using them if you want to set
up the conflict and tone of the book, and if your chapter 1 doesn’t
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
fantasy fantasy settings contain only subtle magical influences. Figure out
which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
* High or Low Fantasy?: High fantasy worlds have pervasive magic. Low
fantasy which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
* Hard vs. Soft Magic Systems: Hard systems have strictly defined
in worldbuilding and storytelling. Let their triumphs inspire your
own.

fantasy fiction! It's an ambitious undertaking, but immensely fulfilling. I
hope these strategies help you turn the fantastical stories kindling in
your soul into fully-realized novels.

Other Fantasy Writing Tips

Here are some final miscellaneous tips that can help you level up as a
fantasy * Prologues: Prologues are slightly controversial, as some authors
don’t like having them, but other authors insist they should be
used. Generally speaking, I recommend using them if you want to set
up the conflict and tone of the book, and if your chapter 1 doesn’t
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
fantasy fantasy settings contain only subtle magical influences. Figure out
which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
do this on its own (common when starting from the “Ordinary
World”.)
* High or Low Fantasy?: High fantasy worlds have pervasive magic. Low
fantasy which mode fits your story best. Low magic often sustains more
tension and sense of wonder when the supernatural is rare.
* Hard vs. Soft Magic Systems: Hard systems have strictly defined
in worldbuilding and storytelling. Let their triumphs inspire your
own.

fantasy fiction! It's an ambitious undertaking, but immensely fulfilling. I
hope these strategies help you turn the fantastical stories kindling in
your soul into fully-realized novels.
